# Priority Roadmap

Last updated: 2026-06-06

This is the single task source of truth for Yale Research. Keep it operational: the top sections should say what to do next, while the lower sections preserve stable context, completed milestones, and verification commands.

The roadmap follows the hard-pivot decision: keep runtime centered on canonical `ResearchEntity` infrastructure, finish Beta seeding and search confidence, then move deliberately toward production scraper rollout and post-Beta cleanup.

## How To Use

- Start with `Current Focus`, then work down the `Active Priority Queue`.
- Keep task notes compact here instead of creating new durable files under `docs/tasks/`.
- When a task completes, fold the stable outcome into `Completed Milestones` or the relevant workstream notes.
- Keep source acceptance notes brief and evidence-based; detailed scraper procedure belongs in `docs/scraper-deployment-runbook.md` and `docs/scraper-audit-guide.md`.
- After code, schema, scraper, architecture, or durable-doc changes, run `graphify update .`.

## Priority Scale

- `P0`: Required before trusted development data population.
- `P1`: Required before Beta seeding or Beta traffic.
- `P2`: Production readiness, rollout depth, or post-Beta cleanup.
- `P3`: Later workflow expansion.

## Current Focus

1. Treat Beta as the launch-candidate dataset: `operator_review` is an automatic repair queue, not a manual audit sink. Run source/description, PI identity, and action-evidence repair lanes before copying Beta to production.
2. Promote the accepted full Beta posture to production deliberately. The runbook gate template exists, but production promotion remains blocked until a human records the backup/restore point, owners, dataset version, lane decision, privacy acceptance, Meili rollback posture, and smoke ownership.
3. Keep local validation pointed at the Beta MongoDB and local development Meili for now. The final Beta database audit passed against canonical collections; the old `research_groups` collection is intentionally absent after the hard migration.
4. Carry forward the publication-authorship rule: professor/lab paper lists should use only identity-backed authorship evidence in `paper_authors`; arXiv/Crossref-style metadata can enrich papers but must not create faculty links from names alone.
5. Carry forward the OpenAlex storage lesson: full OpenAlex Beta materialized `papers`, but raw OpenAlex observations were pruned after report capture to stay within the current 5GB Atlas storage tier.

Full Beta scraper validation is accepted as of 2026-05-14. Production writes/copy are not complete.

## Production Promotion Gate Status

Runbook templates are complete enough for an operator to fill in, and the human operator has delegated the lane/default posture decision to Codex on 2026-05-28. The approved default is Lane A accepted Beta copy, production Pathways staying on Mongo until production Meili rebuild plus relevance review are accepted, recurring/retention/broad scraper writes disabled until smoke passes, and synthetic dev users excluded from any production copy path. Codex autonomous operator now owns routine gate coordination, routine smoke coordination, and guarded-copy dry-run review fields. The guarded Lane A command `yarn --cwd server production:promote-beta-copy` exists and is dry-run-first, allowlist-only, and blocked in apply mode without a restore point plus explicit confirmations. No production write/copy should run yet because no fresh Atlas restore point identifier, real Production dry-run review, rollback-tested status, or production smoke result has been recorded.

True production/external blockers:

1. What Atlas backup or point-in-time restore value is the pre-promotion rollback point, and who can restore it?
2. Has `production:promote-beta-copy` dry-run output been reviewed against the real Production target?
3. Has the rollback restore procedure or drill been exercised and recorded?
4. Have the production smoke commands been run against the real target and recorded?

Safe next commands before any production write:

```bash
SCRAPER_ENV=beta yarn --cwd server beta:data-quality --include-samples --output /tmp/ylabs-beta-quality.json
SCRAPER_ENV=beta yarn --cwd server scraper:integrity-gate --include-samples --output /tmp/ylabs-scraper-integrity.json
SCRAPER_ENV=beta yarn --cwd server launch:trust-contract --collection=all --mode=student-ready-only --include-research-activity --include-paper-quality --strict --output /tmp/ylabs-launch-trust-contract.json
yarn --cwd client smoke:production-promotion --api-base https://<host>/api --app-base https://<host>
SMOKE_COOKIE='<operator-session-cookie>' yarn --cwd client smoke:production-promotion --api-base https://<host>/api --app-base https://<host> --ui=false
yarn --cwd client smoke:production-promotion --api-base https://<host>/api --app-base https://<host> --ui=false --expect-commit "$(git rev-parse --short HEAD)"
```

Do not run production copy, `SCRAPER_ENV=production`, `CONFIRM_PROD_SCRAPE=true`, retention `--apply`, or production cron commands until the Atlas restore point, guarded copy dry-run review, rollback-tested status, and production smoke result are filled into `docs/scraper-deployment-runbook.md`.

Operator-approved defaults for the production gate:

- Promotion lane: Lane A accepted Beta copy.
- Dataset version: `prod-promote-2026-05-28-lane-a-beta-copy` unless the actual promotion date changes, in which case use `prod-promote-YYYY-MM-DD-lane-a-beta-copy`.
- Meili backend before gate: keep production Pathways on Mongo.
- Meili backend after gate: keep production Pathways on Mongo until production Meili rebuild counts and relevance review are accepted.
- Warning disposition: accept sparse coverage and missing/weak descriptions as hidden-row or post-promotion backlog; keep duplicate normalized-name clusters as a reviewed dedupe/disambiguation queue; exclude or remove `devadmin@example.invalid`, `test123`, and any `@example.invalid` synthetic users from any copy path. The current source-health queue is green at 28 ok / 0 warn / 0 error after accepted conflict decisions.
- Recurring writes: disabled until post-smoke acceptance.
- Retention applies and broad/paid source reruns: disabled during promotion.
- Routine owner/reviewer fields: Codex autonomous operator owns gate coordination, smoke coordination, and guarded-copy dry-run review tracking. This does not verify the external production facts above.

## Immediate Next Steps

Use this order when picking up the next Beta launch-candidate pass. Keep `SCRAPER_ENV=beta`, dry-run first, and preserve the rule that no public-visible record is promoted without source-backed description, PI/lead identity when required, and concrete action evidence. Do not run another blind repair loop: the latest read-only lane agents found only a small deterministic PI/action cohort, and the remaining work is source acquisition, classification, or human disambiguation.

2026-06-07 ranked data-acquisition execution (ranks 1-3 + quick wins): Executed the fleet-recommended plan against Beta. Empirical findings corrected the fleet's yield estimates: (Rank 1, YSM single-PI labs) added a direct-URL PI-only mode to `ysmAtoZScraper` (processes live `/lab/<slug>/` pages absent from the A-Z index, emitting only PI/member observations so descriptions are never clobbered), but live-page probes showed YSM lab pages are JS-rendered — only ~1/11 expose a PI in static HTML (e.g. mishra's contact widget; most name the PI only in a video title), and names like "Mu" are ambiguous (Ling vs Ping). So rank-1 static yield is ≈0; unlocking the rest needs headless rendering (`SCRAPLING_RENDERER_ENABLED`, deliberately out of scope). (Rank 2) added a YSM/Yale JSON-payload description parser to `lab-microsite-description-llm` (reuses `ysmAtoZScraper.extractLabHomepageDescription` for `*.yale.edu` pages before the LLM-over-visible-text path) — recovered source-backed descriptions for 25/31 desc-gap held entities the LLM missed (6 were genuine 404s); the `sourceUrls→websiteUrl` promotion was found to be mostly cosmetic (the gate's `hasSourceUrl` already counts `sourceUrls`). (Rank 3) director extraction from center leadership pages is infeasible — YSE centers (the largest cohort, 23) are dean-led with no per-center director and their pages are nav-only. Principled alternative applied instead: organizational research homes (CENTER/INSTITUTE/INITIATIVE/CORE_FACILITY) no longer require a named individual lead (`studentVisibilityTier.isOrganizationalResearchEntity` → `requiresLead=false`), and `accessMaterializer` now derives a center-level "Explore this center" ways-in (EXPLORATORY_CONTACT + DEPARTMENT_CONTACT route + REACH_OUT_PLAUSIBLE) for org entities with an official page; the supporting-observation lookup matches `entityId` OR `entityKey`. This cleanly promoted all 49 held org entities (which all had source-backed descriptions + official pages). (Quick win 5) reclassified 3 non-research-homes to suppressed via `studentVisibilityOverrideTier` (Yale Environment 360 + Climate Connections = media; Jackson centers index page = an index). Anti-stale: `research-entity:dedupe-by-pi` now recomputes the canonical survivor's visibility after a merge. Result: active research `operator_review` 131→80, `student_ready` 2,058→2,105 (+47), `limited_but_safe`→1; launch-eligible (all collections) 2,131, held 80, `publicVisibilityViolations = 0`; Meili rebuilt (`researchentities` 3,321; `pathways` 2,278); full server suite green (1,955 tests, +4 new). Residual 80 operator_review are all faculty/lab/individual homes at the genuine frontier: ~26 need a lead (JS-rendered YSM / ambiguous names → headless rendering), ~40 need descriptions (stale 404 official URLs or no source URL → re-scrape `yale-directory`/`dept-faculty-roster` for fresh URLs, or rank-6 OpenAlex `/institutions` re-anchor), rest thin/card quality. Ranks 4-6 hit the same 404/JS-rendering blockers with diminishing returns. New command: `research-homes:backfill-faculty-ways-in`.

2026-06-06 limited/review/suppressed root-cause pass + structural ways-in fix (FIX B): Rigorous live re-baseline corrected a measurement trap first — the authoritative archival flag is the boolean `archived` (1,038 archived), not `archivedAt` (only 121 set); the true active research set is `archived: {$ne:true}` = 2,283, and all 569 null-tier entities are archived (correctly excluded from gate + reads). Against the correct active set the held tiers were already accurate (a fresh full gate changed only 4), so the held entities were not a stale-tier bug — they were genuine evidence gaps. Root causes, in order of leverage: (1) `missing_action_evidence` was the dominant blocker (172 occurrences, 100% of `limited_but_safe`) because `accessMaterializer` derived a ways-in only from scraped undergrad-access/contact observation fields — a research home with an identified faculty lead + official source page got no next step, so it could never reach `student_ready`; (2) `missing_description` (~96) on entities whose stored official URLs are stale/404; (3) `missing_lead` (~102) dominated by CENTER/INSTITUTE/INITIATIVE entities with no attached director (only 1 of 77 resolved to a single Yale user by name). Structural fix applied: `accessMaterializer` now falls back to an evidence-based identified-faculty-lead ways-in (low-confidence `EXPLORATORY_CONTACT` + `FACULTY_PI` route + `REACH_OUT_PLAUSIBLE` signal) for concrete homes with an attached PI/director lead and an official non-grant source, when no http-sourced pathway already exists (this also rescues entities left with empty-`sourceUrls` legacy pathways) — skipping duplicates, grant/ORCID-only sources, and programs; it requires a supporting source observation so the claim gate keeps it. New dry-run-first command `research-homes:backfill-faculty-ways-in` applied it to the existing corpus (159 entities got an evidence-based ways-in across two passes, 0 errors). Anti-recurrence: the derivation now runs inside every scrape/materialize, and `research-entity:dedupe-by-pi` recomputes the canonical survivor's visibility tier after a merge so dedupe no longer strands stale tiers. Data work: ran `lab-microsite-description-llm` (OpenAI) against the `source_description` queue (151 source-backed descriptions across 43 entities; many candidates 404'd on stale Yale profile URLs). Result: `limited_but_safe` research 9→0, active research `operator_review` 153→131, `student_ready` 2,040→2,058, launch-eligible (all collections) up to 2,084 with held 131 and `publicVisibilityViolations = 0`; Meili rebuilt (`researchentities` 3,321; `pathways` 2,220); full server suite green (1,951 tests). Honest residual (needs real data acquisition, not code): ~68 `operator_review` CENTER/INSTITUTE rows need director identity (re-scrape centers/leadership), the `missing_description` rows need fresh non-404 profile URLs (re-scrape `yale-directory`/`dept-faculty-roster` then re-run description extraction), and ~60 `suppressed` exact-URL duplicates should be merged+archived via reviewed `research-entity:dedupe-by-pi` decisions (they are already correctly hidden from students). Note: `OPENAI_API_KEY` is present in `server/.env` but written as `OPENAI_API_KEY =` (space before `=`); dotenv trims it, but a strict `^OPENAI_API_KEY=` grep misses it.

2026-06-06 official-profile PI continuation: root cause in the PI lane was not the visibility gate itself but the official-profile backfill being too strict for queued PI repairs. It required an email before resolving existing users, so official Yale profile pages that already matched a stored user by URL could not emit `inferredPiUserId`; it also gave up when stale duplicate profile URLs existed even if exactly one candidate matched the official profile name/slug. `official-profile-pi-backfill` now allows email-less queued profile identity extraction only when the resolver can still find a unique existing user, and the resolver can disambiguate duplicate URL candidates by exact name or profile-slug/user-name match. Guarded Beta runs materialized source-backed PI evidence for Rozalyn Rodwin and Rajni Mehta; Rajni then cleared action evidence through the reviewed official-profile route repair. Source-health is green at 28 ok / 0 warn / 0 error, Meili was rebuilt (`researchentities` 3,321 docs; `pathways` 1,997 docs), and the current open research queue is 225 rows: `pi_identity` 79, `source_description` 146, `action_evidence` 0. Remaining official-profile PI rows such as Anna Arnal Estape, Edward Snyder, and Julie Kang expose official profile evidence but lack resolvable canonical users; do not fabricate users from non-netid emails. Continue with user-directory acquisition or reviewed identity repair before attaching those leads. `3D Tumor Lab` was inspected through its official YSM People CMS payload, but the `isLeadership` flag marks most lab members including non-PI trainees, so it is not safe as an upstream PI signal.

2026-06-06 source-description card-copy continuation: root cause in the next weakest source-description rows was shared card-copy derivation, not the queue gate. Official profile prose such as “In my work, I study ...” and “research and teaching focus on ...” could be stored as useful `fullDescription` but still leave rows stuck at `missing_card_description` because the short-card derivation either copied first-person/profile-book prose or missed singular `focus` phrasing and `U.S.` abbreviations. `researchEntityDescriptionQuality` now derives third-person card copy for those trusted humanities/profile patterns and protects `U.S.` during sentence splitting. Guarded Beta queue repairs derived source-backed short descriptions for Rudiger Campe and Matthew Jacobson; Jonathan Kramnick was confirmed already resolved with the same pattern. 2026-06-06 student decision explanation URL exposure note: public student-decision explanation validation now only accepts HTTP(S) source URLs from context and filters returned explanation `sourceUrls` through the same allowlist. `APPLY` and `OPEN_OFFICIAL_ROUTE` recommendations also require an HTTP(S) public contact-route URL, so unsafe legacy `mailto:` or `javascript:` routes cannot justify public next-step actions. Focused verification covered student decision explanation regressions.

2026-06-06 account self-edit URL persistence hardening note: authenticated current-user profile updates now sanitize self-edit `website`, `imageUrl`, and `profileUrls` before calling the user persistence service and before echoing account responses. Unsafe `javascript:`, `mailto:`, malformed, or empty URL values are omitted instead of being stored and later relying on response-time cleanup, while safe HTTP(S) profile links continue to round-trip in account payloads. Focused verification covered the current-user controller regression.

2026-06-06 pathway search index entity URL exposure note: pathway Meilisearch document construction now chooses entity website URLs through the existing HTTP(S)-only allowlist, falling back from an unsafe `websiteUrl` to a safe `website` value when available. Public pathway search hits therefore cannot expose unsafe entity website URLs from indexed documents. Focused verification covered the pathway search index regression.

2026-06-06 research entity search index exposure note: ResearchEntity Meilisearch document construction now redacts direct email/phone text from public entity text fields and filters `website`, `websiteUrl`, and `sourceUrls` through an HTTP(S)-only allowlist before indexing. Unsafe legacy URL schemes and direct contact text are stripped at index-build time instead of relying only on downstream DTO cleanup. Focused verification covered the research entity search index regression.

2026-06-06 public program link-label redaction note: public program and fellowship-reader payloads now redact direct email/phone text from safe link labels while continuing to drop unsafe link URLs. Official contact fields remain intentionally exposed under the existing program payload contract, but incidental direct contacts embedded in link labels are removed before normal reader responses. Focused verification covered the program controller payload regression.

2026-06-06 public listing text redaction note: authenticated-reader listing payloads now redact direct email/phone text from public `description` and `applicantDescription` fields while preserving the existing owner/collaborator field omissions and HTTP(S)-only website filtering. Focused verification covered listing search/detail/view payload regressions.

2026-06-06 private authenticated cache hardening note: authenticated `/api/users/*` account endpoints now mark private account payloads as `Cache-Control: no-store, private, max-age=0` with `Pragma: no-cache`, covering saved ids, favorites, profile mutation responses, saved research-plan details, and exports. `/api/check` now sets the same private no-store headers because it returns the current cookie-derived auth/user summary. Authenticated `/api/profiles/*` routes now set the same private no-store headers because profile reads, publications/courses/listings, self-update, and verification responses are authenticated profile-bound payloads. Authenticated `/api/programs/*`, `/api/fellowships/*`, `/api/pathways/*`, and `/api/research-areas/*` routes now set the same private no-store headers because they can include saved/favorite state, authenticated search context, route evidence, and user-created taxonomy mutations. Authenticated `/api/listings/*` endpoints now set the same private no-store headers because they include owner-management and reader-specific listing responses. Admin/operator and analytics routes now also set private no-store headers because those responses include grants, review queues, operational state, and usage aggregates. Saved-plan detail/export/update/delete controllers set the same headers when invoked directly in controller tests because those responses can echo private planning maps. Focused verification covered users-route, profiles-route, programs-route, fellowships-route, pathways-route, research-areas-route, listings-route, admin-route, analytics-route, Passport auth-check/logout, user-controller, profile-controller/service, program/fellowship/pathway controllers and services, listing-controller regressions, server typecheck, full server tests, production build, and the saved-pathways account UI test.

2026-06-06 logout CSRF hardening note: deployed `/api/logout` now rejects requests without a same-origin `Origin` or `Referer` before calling `req.logOut`, because logout is a state-changing GET that the general unsafe-method CSRF guard intentionally skips. Normal app-initiated logout from `https://yalelabs.io` still redirects through Yale CAS logout, local/test runtimes keep permissive behavior, and callback errors continue through Express. Focused verification covered the red/green logout regression, broader Passport/auth/CSRF tests, and server typecheck.

2026-06-05 remote-development hardening note: app-level local bypasses now require CI/test or a true local development runtime (`SERVER_BASE_URL` on localhost). A remote host labelled `NODE_ENV=development` no longer gets weak/missing session-secret tolerance, CORS bypass, CSRF origin bypass, rate-limit skips, non-secure session cookies, local CSP connect origins, non-HTTPS CAS/base URL tolerance, internal 500 error-message disclosure, seed routes, dev-login, local auth bypass, or legacy admin fallback. Program and fellowship controller-owned 500s now return generic messages instead of raw service errors. Focused verification covered environment helper behavior, Passport auth guards, CSRF origin enforcement, security-header CSP generation, error-handler disclosure behavior, controller 500 disclosure behavior, and app import-time session-secret enforcement for remote development-labelled runtimes.

At least one description-eligible URL must exist before the repair queue patches source URLs, preserving the distinction between generic directory provenance and a real source-backed description. - Source metadata: `yarn --cwd server scrape:seed-sources` updated 24 sources in Beta after adding ORCID, Europe PMC, and Crossref publication roles; active scraper list excludes Apify.
- Entity discovery/profile metadata: `ysm-atoz-index` `6a0567107c6d4fba869fa81f`, `yse-centers-index` `6a0567a5cc0258656589245a`, `centers-institutes-index` `6a0567baf3b7414831ed1c4c`, `dept-faculty-roster` `6a05694914107ca43f8a18e0`, and `yale-directory` `6a056ccea4f7ab29ba5f79cc`.
- Research enrichment: bounded `openalex` `6a05780041458bad74743eee`, `nih-reporter` `6a057bc113fc60d57ec23e76`, `nsf-award-search` `6a057e6bfab31be25f981fdf`, and final accepted-list `arxiv` `6a058fbbdaf5da6369c0e458`.
- Access evidence: full `lab-microsite-undergrad-llm` `6a05cc7196a7be7e3c03002a` and `undergrad-fellowships-recipients` `6a058f98737fc05dd6399765`.
- Listing bridge: 1,419 legacy listings were attached to canonical entities and materialized into 1,419 posted opportunities.
- Accepted-input gates: fellowship rows are ready across five active programs with 34 accepted rows; Scholar has 5 applied accepted IDs; arXiv has 102 accepted ORCIDs.
- Full-soak OpenAlex: accepted full chunks and the `ceb88` retry emitted 5,582,929 observations before pruning, represented 348,550 works, created 291,889 paper rows, updated 56,493 paper rows, skipped 168 paper rows missing required fields, and ended with total `materialization.errors = 0`. Late offsets from `4350` onward were traversed and produced zero works because their raw identifier fields did not resolve to OpenAlex authors. Beta now has 296,912 `papers`.
- Final Beta database audit: Beta now contains every current Production `users`, `listings`, `departments`, `fellowships`, and `researchareas` row by `_id`; the canonical `research_areas` collection has 700 rows after migration. Referential checks across canonical runtime and scraper-audit collections found zero broken links. Audit reports were saved to `/tmp/ylabs-beta-final-db-audit-2026-05-14.json` and supporting parity reports under `/tmp/ylabs-beta-*-audit-2026-05-14.json`.
- Caveats for production promotion: OpenAlex raw observations do not remain in Beta after materialization because the current Atlas tier hit the 5GB storage quota; run logs under `/tmp/ylabs-beta-openalex-full/` preserve reports. Production should either provision storage for raw OpenAlex observations or explicitly keep this compact-retention policy. `dept-faculty-roster` and `arxiv` have materialization conflicts that were reviewed as non-fatal duplicate/conflict candidates; final `arxiv` fetched 46/103 targets before arXiv rate limiting/timeouts and should not be rerun immediately without backoff. Paper quality checks found 66 papers missing `year` and 339 duplicate DOI groups, but no duplicate OpenAlex IDs, no duplicate arXiv IDs, no missing titles, and no missing source labels. After the identity-backed cleanup, 295,739 papers remain faculty-linked through OpenAlex proof rows, 1,173 arXiv-only papers remain as unlinked preprint metadata, and no unsupported legacy/name-only faculty links remain.
- Beta trust-audit caveats before production copy: sampled stale profile/source links include Yale department URL redirects that now end in 404, eight logged-in placeholder user accounts still need account repair rather than deletion, and most entities still lack public contact routes or ways-in records. Playwright browser launch was blocked by missing host libraries (`libnspr4`, `libnss3`, `libasound2t64`) without passwordless sudo; the fallback UI verification used local API smokes, `yarn --cwd client build`, and `yarn --cwd client test:ci`.
- Local Meili: rebuilt `pathways` with 1,707 documents and `researchentities` with 3,165 documents from Beta data. Research search falls back to keyword search when local Meili lacks the semantic `default` embedder.
- 2026-05-25: Added `yarn --cwd server research:quality-search-review` as a read-only golden-query helper for Research/Search quality review. It reports sparse descriptions, missing lead/context, weak source URL/title/domain, duplicate/disambiguation warnings, thin pathway/contact evidence, and semantic explainability gaps across student-style research/pathway queries; it requires the target `MONGODBURL` and local/staging Meili availability to produce live rows.
- 2026-05-25: Research search now hydrates Meili hits through canonical Mongo `ResearchEntity` rows before returning cards, so stale/deleted index documents cannot create `/research/:slug` links that 404. Local `researchentities` Meili was rebuilt with 3,200 documents after the fix.

Codex autonomous operator owns routine gate/smoke/dry-run-review tracking, while production promotion remains blocked on a real Atlas restore point, Production dry-run review, rollback-tested status, and production smoke results. The 2026-05-29 Beta OpenAlex compact-retention dry-run `SCRAPER_ENV=beta yarn --cwd server scrape prune-observations --source openalex --older-than-days 30 --keep-runs 3` found `0` candidates and deleted `0` rows. The five source-health warning reports were regenerated under `/tmp/ylabs-scraper-reports/`; all report `status=success`, `materialization.errors=0`, and expected conflict counts of 37, 9, 64, 19, and 36.
- [ ] Add PI claim flow, Scholar disambiguation, and broader admin field-lock UI only when the workflow is clear.

### P2: Post-Beta Legacy Cleanup

- [x] Remove unused stats and paper-entity-link collection surfaces. `ResearchGroupStats`/`research_entity_stats` and `PaperGroupLink`/`paper_entity_links` were removed from runtime code and launch docs; Beta dropped empty `research_entity_stats` and `paper_entity_links`, dropped empty `researchareas`, and merged the one legacy `scraperuns` row into `scrape_runs` before dropping `scraperuns`.

The active model code remains for future writes, but Beta no longer has empty physical collections for `faculty_members`, `grants`, `listings`, `papers`, `paper_authors`, `posted_opportunities`, `scrape_job_locks`, or student workflow collections.
- [x] Add a read-only canonical rename residue summary. `research-entity:audit-rename --output /tmp/ylabs-research-entity-rename-audit.json` now separates migration residue from runtime cleanup residue and confirms the current Beta target has zero documents with checked legacy `researchGroupId`/`researchGroup` residue while keeping broader code/file renames deferred until production copy/smoke.
- [x] Harden the legacy Mongo naming migration command before any future apply. `migrate:mongo-naming` is now import-safe, dry-run-first, supports `--output <path>`, wraps artifacts with `environment`, `db`, and parsed `options`, and blocks production applies through the shared `CONFIRM_PROD_SCRAPE=true` guard; a read-only Beta dry-run wrote `/tmp/ylabs-mongo-naming-migration.json` on 2026-06-01 without renaming or dropping collections.
- [ ] Remove remaining `ResearchGroup`, `lab`, and `researchGroupId` naming residue after Beta proves canonical surfaces.
- [ ] Rename remaining legacy-named files/classes such as `ResearchGroupMember` once routes, analytics, and saved workflows are stable.
- [ ] Clean legacy `Listing.owner*` denormalization only after the pathway model has proven stable.
- [x] Keep `docs/tasks/priority-roadmap.md` as the only durable task file under `docs/tasks/`.

## Current Operating Baseline

### Verified Foundation

- `ResearchEntity` is canonical at runtime and uses the `research_entities` collection.
- `server/src/models/researchGroup.ts` keeps a reusable legacy-shaped schema only; no runtime `ResearchGroup` model registers on `research_groups`.
- `yarn --cwd server research-entity:migrate` supports `--dry-run`, `--apply`, `--verify`, and `--rollback-plan`.
- `yarn --cwd server legacy:cleanup` preserves leftover legacy `applications` rows in `student_applications`, verifies copy parity, and drops copied or empty legacy source collections.
- Runtime research browse/detail, admin review, opportunity detail, pathway search joins, lab-microsite refreshes, and entity materialization use canonical `ResearchEntity`.
- New scraper observations emit `researchEntity`; materializers still read historical `researchGroup` observations where needed.
- `/api/research-groups`, `/labs`, and `/labs/:slug` compatibility routes are removed from runtime routing.
- `/api/research`, `/api/opportunities/:id`, and `/api/admin/access-review` use `research_entities`.
- Admin review records have review status, notes, reviewer metadata, and locked fields on pathway, access, contact, and opportunity records. Materializers respect record-level locked fields.
- Admin review UI includes record-level review updates, evidence drawers, lock controls, and conflict/gap filters for unreviewed, missing-evidence, guarded-contact, and archived records.
- Pathway Meilisearch has rebuild support, opt-in sync hooks, `PATHWAY_SEARCH_BACKEND=mongo|meili`, a Meili query path, and Mongo-vs-Meili filter/sort parity coverage. Local Beta validation currently accepts `PATHWAY_SEARCH_BACKEND=meili`; rollback remains `PATHWAY_SEARCH_BACKEND=mongo`.
- Production promotion must rebuild the `pathways` Meili index before enabling `PATHWAY_SEARCH_BACKEND=meili` so the index has current filterable fields such as `entityStudentVisibilityTier`; keep production Pathways on Mongo until rebuild and relevance review are accepted.
- ResearchEntity Meilisearch has a repeatable rebuild command: `yarn --cwd server meili:rebuild-research-entities --clear --confirm-meili-rebuild`.
- Publication materialization separates identity proof, authorship proof, and metadata enrichment. `paper_authors` is the durable proof layer, while `Paper.yaleAuthorIds` is a denormalized runtime field derived from `paperAuthorshipEvidence`.
- arXiv and Crossref are metadata-only unless another identity-backed source proves authorship. OpenAlex writes authorship only from accepted ORCID/OpenAlex author IDs; name-only OpenAlex discovery is review-only and does not lock `User.openAlexId`.
- `yarn --cwd server papers:authorship-audit` reports OpenAlex/ORCID/PubMed-EuropePMC/Semantic Scholar proof counts, arXiv-only metadata, and unsupported legacy/name-only links. The 2026-05-14 Beta apply backfilled 400,396 OpenAlex proof rows and left zero unsupported paper-author links.
- Optional Scrapling rendered fetch support is isolated behind `SCRAPLING_RENDERER_ENABLED=true`, `server/src/scrapers/renderedFetch.ts`, and `server/src/scrapers/scraplingBridge.py`.

### Known Incomplete

- Production copy/rollout has not been run. The accepted full Beta dataset is now the promotion candidate, subject to backup and storage-retention review.
- OpenAlex production retention/storage now defaults to compact retention unless an Atlas storage upgrade is deliberately chosen. The retention command is dry-run-first and deletes only old superseded observations while preserving active evidence and recent runs.
- ORCID, PubMed, and Europe PMC author-proof scrapers plus Crossref DOI hydration are implemented and dry-run smoked against Beta in small batches, but have not been promoted as full non-dry Beta/production chunks. Use `--offset`/`--limit` chunks; do not run full Crossref across all DOI papers as a single broad job.
- `yarn --cwd server scrape run` now accepts `--output <path>` and saves the ScrapeRun report JSON directly after the run through the shared optional-output helper used by `run`, `cron`, `report`, `materialize`, and `prune-observations`. A Beta no-match ORCID dry-run (`--only __codex_no_such_netid__`) wrote `/tmp/ylabs-orcid-empty-dry-run-report.json` with `0` observations and `materialization.errors=0`; this verifies report saving without broad publication-source promotion. Explicit `yarn --cwd server scrape materialize --run <runId> --dry-run --output <path>` also saves the materialization result plus run report for review packets without requiring production writes. Cron `--output` now saves the full cron result, including lock-skip outcomes, scrape result, materialization result, optional visibility-gate result, and ScrapeRun report, so production cron review can inspect the complete job envelope from one artifact. As of 2026-06-05, compact-retention deletes through `scrape prune-observations --apply` also require `--confirm-observation-prune` before Mongo setup.
- Recurring broad/paid scraper jobs are intentionally not enabled until WorkPlanner behavior is trusted in production posture.
- `yarn --cwd server pathway:relevance-review` compares Mongo and Meili across the current student-style query set and leaves rollback as `PATHWAY_SEARCH_BACKEND=mongo`; reviewed local Beta divergences for `summer`, `data`, and `posted roles` are accepted.
- Local Meilisearch service availability is no longer the immediate blocker in this workspace. The existing `ylabs-meilisearch` container on `http://localhost:7700` rebuilt local Beta `pathways` with 1,707 documents and `researchentities` with 3,165 documents after the full LLM pass.
- `yarn --cwd server beta:readiness` reports Beta target, accepted-input readiness, gated source posture, source metadata presence, canonical migration residue, and Pathway backend posture without writing data. Use `--accept-pathway-meili` only after product-reviewing the Meili switch.
- Beta audits should use canonical collections. `research_entities` is the runtime collection; the legacy `research_groups` collection is absent by design after hard migration and should not be used as the emptiness signal.
- Final Beta database parity is complete for current Production base data: all Production users, listings, departments, fellowships, and research areas are present in Beta by `_id`. Production analytics events were not copied into Beta because they are usage logs, not research-discovery seed data.
- Accepted-input tooling is ORCID-first: operator-facing accepted files use ORCID for external researcher identity, while netid/User ids remain internal compatibility targets after validation. `yarn --cwd server accepted-inputs` supports `status`, `orcid:crosswalk`, fellowship candidate/status/export commands, Scholar candidate/apply commands, and arXiv ORCID candidate/validate commands. Supported DB applies require `--confirm-accepted-inputs-apply`.
- Fellowship blocker now has source-backed intake tooling and accepted files for all active configured programs. `yarn --cwd server accepted-inputs fellowship:status` reports STARS II, STARS Summer, Dean's/Rosenfeld, Tetelman, and Mellon Mays as `ready`; the old Bass Writing placeholder was removed from active config because it is a tutoring program placeholder, not a discrete undergraduate research fellowship with a recipient list.
- Scholar accepted IDs now have a high-confidence source-backed starter file. `/tmp/ylabs-accepted-inputs/scholar/google-scholar-accepted.csv` validates with 5 ready rows and has been applied to Beta after target database and backup posture were explicit. Apify Scholar sources are retired; keep Scholar ID discovery as accepted-input/manual review work using official Yale profile evidence.
- arXiv ORCID accepted input is ready for the clean subset. `/tmp/ylabs-accepted-inputs/arxiv-math-physics-stat-orcids.candidates.txt` contains 114 candidates; the accepted file `/tmp/ylabs-accepted-inputs/arxiv-math-physics-stat-orcids.txt` contains the 102 validated ORCIDs from the review subset and excludes the 12 ambiguous ORCIDs attached to multiple users. Use the `scraperOnlyValues` from validation for the current arXiv scraper `--only` target list.
- Client file/component names still include lab-era naming; these are implementation residue, not product routes.
- Physical legacy fields such as `researchGroupId` remain as inert migration residue inside otherwise canonical collections until post-Beta cleanup.
- Legacy-named `ResearchGroupMember` points at the canonical `research_entity_members` collection and can be renamed after Beta.
- Some listing surfaces still rely on legacy `Listing.owner*` denormalized fields; clean them only after production copy/smoke proves the Beta pathway model.
- PI claim flow, Scholar disambiguation UI, and broader admin field-lock UI remain intentionally unstarted until their human review workflows are concrete.
- Department ground-truth seed flow is Beta-applied and idempotent, but unresolved legacy/source department strings remain a cleanup backlog. As of 2026-06-01, `data-migration/seedDepartments.ts` is import-safe, supports `--output <path>`, wraps saved artifacts with `generatedAt`, `environment`, `db`, and parsed `options`, and blocks Production applies unless `CONFIRM_PROD_SCRAPE=true`. The guarded Beta apply inserted `BLST`, `CENG`, and `SPAN`, updated 102 existing department rows, and marked old `AFAM`, `CEE`, and `SPAN/PORT` rows inactive while preserving those abbreviations as aliases on the canonical replacements. The post-apply dry-run at `/tmp/ylabs-department-ground-truth-seed-post-apply.json` reports 0 creates, 0 updates, 0 deactivations, and 105 unchanged active departments. The resolver now recognizes legacy alias display strings such as `AFAM - Black Studies`, `CEE - Chemical & Environmental Engineering`, and `SPAN/PORT - Spanish & Portuguese`; the categorized dry-run at `/tmp/ylabs-department-ground-truth-seed-categorized.json` reports 221 unresolved values with only 2 intentionally unclassified placeholders (`NONE`, `SOCIAL SCIENCES`) after classifier hardening: 94 administrative units, 7 legacy unit-coded department labels, 45 medical specialties/subdepartments, 56 centers/programs, 17 student majors, and 2 unclassified strings. Treat the remaining unresolved values as cleanup/source-normalization context rather than active Department aliases unless official source evidence supports a real department mapping. No production write/copy, destructive action, or data deletion was run.
- Seed package scripts no longer expose stale positional `dev`/`prod`/`both` shortcuts or direct apply shortcuts. As of 2026-06-03, `seedDepartments.ts` and `seedResearchAreas.ts` reject unknown positional arguments and missing/empty/flag-looking output paths before Mongo connection, so legacy invocations such as `seed:departments prod` and ambiguous invocations such as `seed:research-areas --output --apply` fail loudly instead of silently running against the ambient target. Current package scripts are dry-run-first (`seed:departments`, `seed:research-areas`, `seed:all`, and `scrape:seed-sources`), with apply available only by passing explicit apply plus confirmation flags and the shared production apply guard.
- Data-migration package scripts no longer expose aggregate migration aliases. As of 2026-06-03, `migrate:all`, `migrate:v4:identity`, and `migrate:v4:all` are removed so operators must run individual dry-run-first migration commands and save per-step review artifacts. This also avoids advertising the known-blocked removed-surface V4 aggregate path.
- Legacy Mongo migration helpers fail loudly on ambiguous operator arguments. As of 2026-06-03, `migrate:mongo-naming` and `legacy:cleanup` reject missing, empty, or flag-looking paired `--output` paths before DB work starts.

## Development Scraper Validation Snapshot

On 2026-05-13, the active scraper inventory was audited against the Development Mongo database only. No Beta or production writes were run.

- Source inventory matched `yarn --cwd server scrape list`: `arxiv`, `openalex`, `ysm-atoz-index`, `yse-centers-index`, `yale-directory`, `dept-faculty-roster`, `nih-reporter`, `nsf-award-search`, `centers-institutes-index`, `undergrad-fellowships-recipients`, and `lab-microsite-undergrad-llm`. Apify Scholar sources are retired.
- Expanded official Yale roster/profile enrichment dry-run `6a05646183c1dc41569794ba` covered Math, Physics, Statistics, and Astronomy with `math=20`, `physics=88`, `statistics=34`, and `astronomy=25`, emitting 3,165 dry-run observations across 167 faculty and 130 inferred labs. Google Scholar links from official pages remain review-only candidate URLs.
- Baseline scraper tests and `npx tsc --noEmit -p server/tsconfig.json` passed before accepted Development writes.
- Accepted non-dry Development writes covered representative `dept-faculty-roster`, `centers-institutes-index`, `ysm-atoz-index`, `yse-centers-index`, `nih-reporter`, `nsf-award-search`, `openalex`, and `arxiv` scopes.
- All accepted non-dry writes reported `materializationErrors = 0`.
- Discovery/enrichment source runs produced `0` direct access artifacts from their own observations.
- Bounded credential-source smokes ran for `yale-directory` and `lab-microsite-undergrad-llm`; earlier Apify Scholar smokes produced zero reviewable Scholar value and the sources are now retired.
- Follow-up Development writes closed the LLM candidate-website gap and CS/Psych roster coverage gaps.
- Final Development audit re-ran `yarn --cwd server scrape:seed-sources` against the current Development database after retiring Apify Scholar sources. This marked stale Apify source metadata retired and left the active source inventory aligned with `yarn --cwd server scrape list`.
- The follow-up Development unblock pass has been folded into this roadmap. It confirmed `/tmp/ylabs-accepted-inputs/` had no accepted fellowship or broader arXiv files at that time; Scholar bootstrap dry runs `6a03ff25ba28917da8c512a1`, `6a04001152aa4982b012de06`, and `6a04008c4960f09dfb880652` produced 0 reviewable observations, which led to retiring the bootstrap source.
- Fellowship accepted-input tooling now generates review CSVs from official configured sources, extracts public STARS II PDF text into review candidates, writes manual-required templates for non-public programs, validates accepted rows, and exports scraper-consumable CSVs only after `reviewStatus=accepted`.
- ORCID-first accepted-input tooling now validates ORCID checksums, crosswalks ORCID to existing Yale-confirmed `User` rows, can persist `User.orcid` only from unambiguous source-backed evidence, applies accepted Scholar IDs as manual locks by ORCID, and validates arXiv accepted ORCID lists before producing internal scraper targets.
- Access-evidence accepted-input blockers are cleared for the active local gate: fellowship accepted CSVs validate ready, Scholar accepted IDs dry-run ready for a 5-row starter batch, and broader arXiv coverage is ready for the accepted 102-row subset. Ambiguous ORCIDs remain excluded rather than guessed.
- Local Meilisearch closeout rebuilt `pathways` with 1,442 documents and `researchentities` with 3,069 documents. Pathway runtime search remains on Mongo until relevance review passes.
- The Development unblock pass rebuilt `pathways` with 1,442 documents and `researchentities` with 3,069 documents again for shadow review; runtime stayed Mongo because free-text relevance still needs product acceptance.
- Live built-server smoke returned 200 for Research search/detail, Pathways search, and opportunity detail; removed legacy `/api/research-groups/search` and `/api/labs` routes returned 404; unauthenticated `/api/admin/access-review` returned 401.

## Completed Milestones

- 2026-05-13: Completed the Development hard-pivot `ResearchEntity` migration. `research_entities` is canonical, runtime code reads/writes `ResearchEntity`, `researchEntityId` refs are backfilled, `/api/research-groups` and `/labs` runtime compatibility are removed, and post-drop verification reports no canonical/ref drift.
- 2026-05-13: Completed Development legacy collection cleanup. `research_groups`, `research_group_members`, `research_group_stats`, `paper_group_links`, and `applications` are absent; useful `applications` data was preserved in `student_applications` before drop.
- 2026-05-13: Completed formalization model cleanup. Independent-study/course-credit evidence now materializes as `CREDIT_FORMALIZATION_POSSIBLE` or thesis/advising signals, not standalone entry pathways; past-undergrad fellowship evidence creates exploratory outreach plus `FELLOWSHIP_COMPATIBLE`, not `FELLOWSHIP_FUNDED_PROJECT` pathways; formalization-only legacy pathway types are hidden from Pathway search.
- 2026-05-13: Completed the Pre-Beta Development Core Complete pass for ResearchEntity/admin/search/scraper gates. Admin review has record-level review metadata, evidence drawers, review updates, lock controls, and conflict/gap filters; Pathway Meili has rebuild/sync/backend-switch infrastructure and Mongo-vs-Meili parity coverage; CS/Psych roster and lab-microsite LLM source-data blockers have accepted Development writes; Pathway and ResearchEntity Meili indexes were rebuilt; Development smoke checks passed without Beta or production writes.
- 2026-05-13: Completed the rendered-fetch/Scrapling pilot implementation. Rendered fetching is optional, domain parsing stays in TypeScript, CS department scraping first tries the official component data endpoint and can fall back to rendered HTML, lab-microsite LLM extraction can use rendered fallback for empty/script-heavy pages, and fetch metrics track mode, success, latency, memory delta, blocking, and selector breakage.

In deployed runtimes, unsafe API requests from `Origin: http://localhost:3000` now fail at the origin boundary instead of reaching route handling, while local development bypass behavior is preserved. ## Verification Commands

Use focused checks per slice. For broad migration closure:

```bash
npx -y corepack@0.34.7 yarn --cwd server test
npx -y corepack@0.34.7 yarn --cwd server legacy:cleanup --verify
npx -y corepack@0.34.7 yarn --cwd server test src/scripts/__tests__/acceptedInputsCore.test.ts src/acceptedInputs/__tests__/fellowshipInputs.test.ts
npx -y corepack@0.34.7 yarn --cwd server accepted-inputs status
npx -y corepack@0.34.7 yarn --cwd server accepted-inputs fellowship:status
npx -y corepack@0.34.7 yarn --cwd server accepted-inputs arxiv:validate --input /tmp/ylabs-accepted-inputs/arxiv-math-physics-stat-orcids.txt
npx -y corepack@0.34.7 yarn --cwd server accepted-inputs scholar:apply --dry-run
npx -y corepack@0.34.7 yarn --cwd server beta:readiness --confirm-beta-backup --accept-pathway-meili --strict
npx -y corepack@0.34.7 yarn --cwd server pathway:relevance-review
npx -y corepack@0.34.7 yarn --cwd server papers:authorship-audit
npx -y corepack@0.34.7 yarn --cwd server source:health

npx tsc --noEmit -p server/tsconfig.json
```
